 <P STYLE="margin-top:0pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman"><B>Item&nbsp;2.02&nbsp;Results of Operations and Financial Condition </B></P>
<P STYLE="margin-top:6pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">On January&nbsp;17, 2017, United Continental Holdings, Inc. (&#147;UAL&#148;), the holding company whose primary subsidiary is United Airlines, Inc.
(&#147;United,&#148; and together with UAL, the &#147;Company&#148;), issued a press release announcing the financial results of the Company for fourth quarter and full year 2016. The press release is attached as Exhibit 99.1 and is incorporated
herein by reference. </P> <P STYLE="margin-top:12pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">The information in this Item&nbsp;2.02, including Exhibit 99.1, is being furnished and shall not be deemed to be &#147;filed&#148;
for purposes of Section&nbsp;18 of the Securities Exchange Act of 1934, as amended (the &#147;Exchange Act&#148;) or otherwise subject to the liabilities of that Section&nbsp;and shall not be deemed incorporated by reference into any registration
statement or other document filed pursuant to the Securities Act of 1933, as amended (the &#147;Securities Act&#148;) except as shall be expressly set forth by specific reference in such filing. </P>
<P STYLE="margin-top:18pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman"><B>Item&nbsp;7.01&nbsp;Regulation FD Disclosure </B></P> <P STYLE="margin-top:6pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">On
January&nbsp;17, 2017, UAL will provide an investor update related to the financial and operational outlook for the Company for first quarter and full year 2017. A copy of the investor update is attached as Exhibit 99.2 and is incorporated herein by
reference. </P> <P STYLE="margin-top:12pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">The information in this Item&nbsp;7.01, including Exhibit&nbsp;99.2, is being furnished and shall not be deemed to be &#147;filed&#148; for
purposes of Section&nbsp;18 of the Exchange Act or otherwise subject to the liabilities of that Section&nbsp;and shall not be deemed incorporated by reference into any registration statement or other document filed pursuant to the Securities Act
except as shall be expressly set forth by specific reference in such filing. </P> <P STYLE="margin-top:18pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman"><B>Item&nbsp;9.01&nbsp;Financial Statements and Exhibits. </B></P>
<P STYLE="font-size:12pt;margin-top:0pt;margin-bottom:0pt">&nbsp;</P>

</TABLE> <P STYLE="margin-top:0pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:18pt; font-family:Times New Roman" ALIGN="center"><B>United Airlines Reports Full-Year and </B></P>
<P STYLE="margin-top:0pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:18pt; font-family:Times New Roman" ALIGN="center"><B><U>Fourth-Quarter 2016 Performance</U> </B></P>
<P STYLE="margin-top:12pt; margin-bottom:0pt; text-indent:4%; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman"><B>CHICAGO, Jan. 17, 2017</B> &#150; United Airlines (UAL) today announced its fourth-quarter and full-year 2016 financial results. </P>
<P STYLE="font-size:6pt;margin-top:0pt;margin-bottom:0pt">&nbsp;</P>
<TABLE STYLE="BORDER-COLLAPSE:COLLAPSE; font-family:Times New Roman; font-size:10pt" BORDER="0" CELLPADDING="0" CELLSPACING="0" WIDTH="100%">
<TR>
<TD WIDTH="5%">&nbsp;</TD>
<TD WIDTH="2%" VALIGN="top" ALIGN="left">&#149;</TD>
<TD WIDTH="1%" VALIGN="top">&nbsp;</TD>
<TD ALIGN="left" VALIGN="top">Achieved best full-year <FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">on-time</FONT> performance while reporting the lowest number of cancellations, delay minutes and mishandled bags in company history. </TD></TR></TABLE>
<P STYLE="font-size:6pt;margin-top:0pt;margin-bottom:0pt">&nbsp;</P>
<TABLE STYLE="BORDER-COLLAPSE:COLLAPSE; font-family:Times New Roman; font-size:10pt" BORDER="0" CELLPADDING="0" CELLSPACING="0" WIDTH="100%">
<TR>
<TD WIDTH="5%">&nbsp;</TD>
<TD WIDTH="2%" VALIGN="top" ALIGN="left">&#149;</TD>
<TD WIDTH="1%" VALIGN="top">&nbsp;</TD>
<TD ALIGN="left" VALIGN="top">UAL reported full-year net income of $2.3&nbsp;billion, diluted earnings per share of $6.85, <FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">pre-tax</FONT> earnings of $3.8&nbsp;billion and
<FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">pre-tax</FONT> margin of 10.4&nbsp;percent. Excluding special items, UAL reported full-year net income of $2.9&nbsp;billion, diluted earnings per share of $8.65, <FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">pre-tax</FONT>
earnings of $4.5&nbsp;billion and <FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">pre-tax</FONT> margin of 12.2&nbsp;percent. </TD></TR></TABLE> <P STYLE="font-size:6pt;margin-top:0pt;margin-bottom:0pt">&nbsp;</P>
<TABLE STYLE="BORDER-COLLAPSE:COLLAPSE; font-family:Times New Roman; font-size:10pt" BORDER="0" CELLPADDING="0" CELLSPACING="0" WIDTH="100%">
<TR>
<TD WIDTH="5%">&nbsp;</TD>
<TD WIDTH="2%" VALIGN="top" ALIGN="left">&#149;</TD>
<TD WIDTH="1%" VALIGN="top">&nbsp;</TD>
<TD ALIGN="left" VALIGN="top">UAL reported fourth-quarter net income of $397&nbsp;million, diluted earnings per share of $1.26, <FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">pre-tax</FONT> earnings of $884&nbsp;million and
<FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">pre-tax</FONT> margin of 9.8&nbsp;percent. Excluding special items, UAL reported fourth-quarter net income of $562&nbsp;million, diluted earnings per share of $1.78, <FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">pre-tax</FONT>
earnings of $857&nbsp;million and <FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">pre-tax</FONT> margin of 9.5&nbsp;percent. </TD></TR></TABLE> <P STYLE="font-size:6pt;margin-top:0pt;margin-bottom:0pt">&nbsp;</P>
<TABLE STYLE="BORDER-COLLAPSE:COLLAPSE; font-family:Times New Roman; font-size:10pt" BORDER="0" CELLPADDING="0" CELLSPACING="0" WIDTH="100%">
<TR>
<TD WIDTH="5%">&nbsp;</TD>
<TD WIDTH="2%" VALIGN="top" ALIGN="left">&#149;</TD>
<TD WIDTH="1%" VALIGN="top">&nbsp;</TD>
<TD ALIGN="left" VALIGN="top">Technicians and related employees ratified a joint contract in the fourth quarter. UAL has completed new agreements with every domestic unionized work group in 2016. </TD></TR></TABLE>
<P STYLE="font-size:6pt;margin-top:0pt;margin-bottom:0pt">&nbsp;</P>
<TABLE STYLE="BORDER-COLLAPSE:COLLAPSE; font-family:Times New Roman; font-size:10pt" BORDER="0" CELLPADDING="0" CELLSPACING="0" WIDTH="100%">
<TR>
<TD WIDTH="5%">&nbsp;</TD>
<TD WIDTH="2%" VALIGN="top" ALIGN="left">&#149;</TD>
<TD WIDTH="1%" VALIGN="top">&nbsp;</TD>
<TD ALIGN="left" VALIGN="top">Employees earned $628&nbsp;million in profit sharing for 2016. </TD></TR></TABLE> <P STYLE="margin-top:12pt; margin-bottom:0pt; text-indent:4%; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">&#147;Our fourth quarter
financial and operating performance capped an outstanding year for United Airlines,&#148; said Oscar Munoz, chief executive officer of United Airlines. &#147;In 2016 we put into action our plan to become the best airline in the world and last
year&#146;s results demonstrate we are on our way to achieving that ambition. We will continue delivering on this commitment by investing in our employees, elevating our customer experience and driving strong and consistent returns for our
shareholders.&#148;</P> <P STYLE="margin-top:18pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman" ALIGN="center"><B>Full-Year and Fourth-Quarter Revenue </B></P>
<P STYLE="margin-top:6pt; margin-bottom:0pt; text-indent:4%; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">For the fourth quarter of 2016, total revenue was $9.1&nbsp;billion, an increase of 0.2&nbsp;percent year-over-year. Fourth-quarter 2016
consolidated passenger revenue per available seat mile (PRASM) decreased 1.6&nbsp;percent and consolidated yield decreased 1.2&nbsp;percent compared to the fourth quarter of 2015. This outperformance versus the company&#146;s initial guidance was
due to stronger <FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">close-in</FONT> bookings and yields in November and </P>
 <p STYLE="margin-top:0pt;margin-bottom:0pt ; font-size:8pt">&nbsp;</P> <P STYLE="margin-top:0pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman" ALIGN="center">1 </P>


<p Style='page-break-before:always'>
<HR  SIZE="3" style="COLOR:#999999" WIDTH="100%" ALIGN="CENTER">


 <P STYLE="margin-top:0pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">United Airlines Reports Full-Year and Fourth-Quarter 2016 Performance </P>
<p STYLE="margin-top:0pt;margin-bottom:0pt ; font-size:8pt">&nbsp;</P>
 <P STYLE="margin-top:0pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">
December. For the full-year 2016, consolidated PRASM declined 5.4&nbsp;percent compared to the prior year driven by factors including a strong U.S. dollar, lower surcharges, reductions from
energy-related corporate travel, and declining yields. </P> <P STYLE="margin-top:12pt; margin-bottom:0pt; text-indent:4%; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">&#147;We saw meaningful improvement in the pricing and demand environment in the
quarter,&#148; said Scott Kirby, president of United Airlines. &#147;Looking forward, we anticipate first quarter consolidated unit revenues to be approximately flat, marking the fourth straight quarter of sequential quarter-over-quarter
improvement.&#148; </P> <P STYLE="margin-top:18pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman" ALIGN="center"><B>Full-Year and Fourth-Quarter Costs </B></P>
<P STYLE="margin-top:6pt; margin-bottom:0pt; text-indent:4%; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">Total operating expense was $8.0&nbsp;billion in the fourth quarter, up 1.2&nbsp;percent year-over-year. Excluding special charges, total
operating expense was $8.1&nbsp;billion, a 3.2&nbsp;percent increase year-over-year. Consolidated unit cost (CASM) decreased 0.8&nbsp;percent compared to the fourth quarter of 2015 due mainly to lower fuel expense. Fourth quarter consolidated CASM,
excluding special charges, third-party business expenses, fuel and profit sharing, increased 4.1&nbsp;percent year-over-year driven largely by the impact of labor agreements ratified in 2016. For the full year, consolidated CASM decreased
2.9&nbsp;percent compared to the full year 2015 due to lower fuel expense. Excluding special charges, third-party business expenses, fuel and profit sharing, consolidated CASM increased 2.8&nbsp;percent compared to the prior year due primarily to
new labor agreements. </P> <P STYLE="margin-top:12pt; margin-bottom:0pt; text-indent:4%; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">&#147;I am very pleased with core cost performance achieved in the fourth quarter and full-year 2016 where we kept <FONT
STYLE="white-space:nowrap">non-fuel</FONT> cost growth excluding new labor deals nearly constant,&#148; said Andrew Levy, executive vice president and chief financial officer of United Airlines. &#147;I have great confidence we will achieve our cost
efficiency targets outlined at our investor day as we look to offset rising fuel and labor costs.&#148; </P> <P STYLE="margin-top:18pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman" ALIGN="center"><B>Liquidity and Capital
Allocation </B></P> <P STYLE="margin-top:6pt; margin-bottom:0pt; text-indent:4%; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">In the fourth quarter, UAL generated $658&nbsp;million in operating cash flow and ended the quarter with $5.8&nbsp;billion
in unrestricted liquidity, including $1.35&nbsp;billion of undrawn commitments under its revolving credit facility. UAL generated $5.5&nbsp;billion in operating cash flow for the full year. The company continued to invest in its business through
capital expenditures of $880&nbsp;million in the fourth quarter and a total of $3.2&nbsp;billion for the full year. Including assets acquired through the issuance of debt and airport construction financing and excluding fully reimbursable projects,
the company invested $1.1&nbsp;billion during the fourth quarter and $3.3&nbsp;billion for the full year in adjusted capital expenditures. Free cash flow, measured as operating cash flow less adjusted capital expenditures, was $2.2&nbsp;billion for
the full year. </P> <P STYLE="margin-top:12pt; margin-bottom:0pt; text-indent:4%; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">For the 12 months ended Dec. 31, 2016, the company&#146;s return on invested capital was 19.3&nbsp;percent. In the
quarter, UAL purchased $156&nbsp;million of its common shares. For the full year 2016, the company purchased $2.6&nbsp;billion of its common shares, representing approximately 14&nbsp;percent of shares outstanding, at an average price of $51.80 per
share. As of Dec. 31, 2016, the company had $1.8&nbsp;billion remaining to purchase shares under its existing share repurchase authority. </P>
<P STYLE="margin-top:12pt; margin-bottom:0pt; text-indent:4%; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">For more information on UAL&#146;s first-quarter 2017 guidance, please visit ir.united.com for the company&#146;s investor update. </P>
 <p STYLE="margin-top:0pt;margin-bottom:0pt ; font-size:8pt">&nbsp;</P> <P STYLE="margin-top:0pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman" ALIGN="center">2 </P>

<P STYLE="margin-top:6pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman" ALIGN="center"><I>Operations and Employees </I></P> <P STYLE="font-size:6pt;margin-top:0pt;margin-bottom:0pt">&nbsp;</P>

 <P STYLE="margin-top:0pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">United Airlines Reports Full-Year and Fourth-Quarter 2016 Performance </P>
<p STYLE="margin-top:0pt;margin-bottom:0pt ; font-size:8pt">&nbsp;</P>
 <P STYLE="margin-top:0pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman" ALIGN="center"><B>About United </B></P>
<P STYLE="margin-top:6pt; margin-bottom:0pt; text-indent:4%; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">United Airlines and United Express operate more than 4,500 flights a day to 339 airports across five continents. In 2016, United and United
Express operated more than 1.6&nbsp;million flights carrying more than 143&nbsp;million customers. United is proud to have the world&#146;s most comprehensive route network, including U.S. mainland hubs in Chicago, Denver, Houston, Los Angeles, New
York/Newark, San Francisco and Washington, D.C. United operates 737 mainline aircraft and the airline&#146;s United Express partners operate 483 regional aircraft. The airline is a founding member of Star Alliance, which provides service to 192
countries via 28 member airlines. For more information, visit united.com, follow @United on Twitter or connect on Facebook. The common stock of United&#146;s parent, United Continental Holdings, Inc., is traded on the NYSE under the symbol
&#147;UAL&#148;. </P> <P STYLE="margin-top:18pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman"><B>Safe Harbor Statement under the Private Securities Litigation Reform Act of 1995: </B></P>
<P STYLE="margin-top:6pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">Certain statements included in this release are forward-looking and thus reflect our current expectations and beliefs with respect to certain current and
future events and anticipated financial and operating performance. Such forward-looking statements are and will be subject to many risks and uncertainties relating to our operations and business environment that may cause actual results to differ
materially from any future results expressed or implied in such forward-looking statements. Words such as &#147;expects,&#148; &#147;will,&#148; &#147;plans,&#148; &#147;anticipates,&#148; &#147;indicates,&#148; &#147;believes,&#148;
&#147;forecast,&#148; &#147;guidance,&#148; &#147;outlook&#148; and similar expressions are intended to identify forward-looking statements. Additionally, forward-looking statements include statements that do not relate solely to historical facts,
such as statements which identify uncertainties or trends, discuss the possible future effects of current known trends or uncertainties or which indicate that the future effects of known trends or uncertainties cannot be predicted, guaranteed or
assured. All forward-looking statements in this release are based upon information available to us on the date of this release. We undertake no obligation to publicly update or revise any forward-looking statement, whether as a result of new
information, future events, changed circumstances or otherwise, except as required by applicable law. Our actual results could differ materially from these forward-looking statements due to numerous factors including, without limitation, the
following: our ability to comply with the terms of our various financing arrangements; the costs and availability of financing; our ability to maintain adequate liquidity; our ability to execute our operational plans and revenue-generating
initiatives, including optimizing our revenue; our ability to control our costs, including realizing benefits from our resource optimization efforts, revenue-generating initiatives, cost reduction initiatives and fleet replacement programs; our
ability to utilize our net operating losses; our ability to attract and retain customers; demand for transportation in the markets in which we operate; an outbreak of a disease that affects travel demand or travel behavior; demand for travel and the
impact that global economic conditions have on customer travel patterns; excessive taxation and the inability to offset future taxable income; general economic conditions (including interest rates, foreign currency exchange rates, investment or
credit market conditions, crude oil prices, costs of aircraft fuel and energy refining capacity in relevant markets); economic and political instability and other risks of doing business globally; any potential realized or unrealized gains or losses
related to fuel or currency hedging programs; the effects of any hostilities, act of war or terrorist attack; the ability of other air carriers with whom we have alliances or partnerships to provide the services contemplated by the respective
arrangements with such carriers; disruptions to our regional network; the costs and availability of aviation and other insurance; industry consolidation or changes in airline alliances; competitive pressures on pricing and on demand; our capacity
decisions and the capacity decisions of our competitors; U.S. or foreign governmental legislation, regulation and other actions (including Open Skies agreements and environmental regulations); the impact of regulatory, investigative and legal
proceedings and legal compliance risks; the impact of any management changes; labor costs; our ability to maintain satisfactory labor relations and the results of any collective bargaining agreement process with our union groups; any disruptions to
operations due to any potential actions by our labor groups; weather conditions; and other risks and uncertainties set forth under Part I, Item 1A., &#147;Risk Factors,&#148; of UAL&#146;s Annual Report on Form
<FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">10-K</FONT> for the fiscal year ended December&nbsp;31, 2015, as well as other risks and uncertainties set forth from time to time in the reports we file with the U.S. Securities and Exchange Commission. </P>

 <p STYLE="margin-top:0pt;margin-bottom:0pt ; font-size:8pt">&nbsp;</P> <P STYLE="margin-top:0pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman" ALIGN="center">7 </P>


<p Style='page-break-before:always'>
<HR  SIZE="3" style="COLOR:#999999" WIDTH="100%" ALIGN="CENTER">


 <P STYLE="margin-top:0pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">United Airlines Reports Full-Year and Fourth-Quarter 2016 Performance </P>
<p STYLE="margin-top:0pt;margin-bottom:0pt ; font-size:8pt">&nbsp;</P>
 <P STYLE="margin-top:0pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman" ALIGN="center"><B>UNITED CONTINENTAL HOLDINGS, INC. </B></P>
<P STYLE="margin-top:0pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman" ALIGN="center">RETURN ON INVESTED CAPITAL (ROIC) </P> <P STYLE="margin-top:12pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">ROIC is a <FONT
STYLE="white-space:nowrap">Non-GAAP</FONT> financial measure that we believe provides useful supplemental information for management and investors by measuring the effectiveness of our operations&#146; use of invested capital to generate profits.
</P> <P STYLE="font-size:12pt;margin-top:0pt;margin-bottom:0pt">&nbsp;</P>
<TABLE CELLSPACING="0" CELLPADDING="0" WIDTH="100%" BORDER="0" STYLE="BORDER-COLLAPSE:COLLAPSE; font-family:Times New Roman; font-size:10pt" ALIGN="center">

 <p STYLE="margin-top:0pt;margin-bottom:0pt ; font-size:8pt">&nbsp;</P> <P STYLE="margin-top:0pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman" ALIGN="center">8 </P>


<p Style='page-break-before:always'>
<HR  SIZE="3" style="COLOR:#999999" WIDTH="100%" ALIGN="CENTER">


 <P STYLE="margin-top:0pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">United Airlines Reports Full-Year and Fourth-Quarter 2016 Performance </P>
<p STYLE="margin-top:0pt;margin-bottom:0pt ; font-size:8pt">&nbsp;</P>
 <P STYLE="margin-top:0pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman" ALIGN="center"><B>UNITED CONTINENTAL HOLDINGS, INC. </B></P>
<P STYLE="margin-top:0pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman" ALIGN="center"><FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">NON-GAAP</FONT> FINANCIAL RECONCILIATION </P>
<P STYLE="margin-top:12pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">(A) Pursuant to SEC Regulation G, UAL has included the following reconciliations of reported <FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">Non-GAAP</FONT> financial
measures to comparable financial measures reported on a GAAP basis. </P> <P STYLE="margin-top:12pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">CASM is a common metric used in the airline industry to measure an airline&#146;s
cost structure and efficiency. UAL reports CASM excluding special charges, third-party business expenses, fuel and profit sharing. UAL believes that adjusting for special charges is useful to investors because special charges are <FONT
STYLE="white-space:nowrap">non-recurring</FONT> charges not indicative of UAL&#146;s ongoing performance. UAL also believes that excluding third-party business expenses, such as maintenance, ground handling and catering services for third parties,
fuel sales and <FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">non-air</FONT> mileage redemptions, provides more meaningful disclosure because these expenses are not directly related to UAL&#146;s core business. UAL also believes that excluding fuel costs from
certain measures is useful to investors because it provides an additional measure of management&#146;s performance excluding the effects of a significant cost item over which management has limited influence. UAL excludes profit sharing because this
exclusion allows investors to better understand and analyze our recurring cost performance and provides a more meaningful comparison of our core operating costs to the airline industry. In addition, the company believes that adjusting for MTM gains
and losses from fuel derivative contracts settling in future periods and prior period gains and losses on fuel derivative contracts settled in the current period is useful because the adjustments allow investors to better understand the cash impact
of settled fuel derivative contracts in a given period. </P> <P STYLE="font-size:12pt;margin-top:0pt;margin-bottom:0pt">&nbsp;</P>
<TABLE CELLSPACING="0" CELLPADDING="0" WIDTH="100%" BORDER="0" STYLE="BORDER-COLLAPSE:COLLAPSE; font-family:Times New Roman; font-size:10pt" ALIGN="center">

 <p STYLE="margin-top:0pt;margin-bottom:0pt ; font-size:8pt">&nbsp;</P> <P STYLE="margin-top:0pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman" ALIGN="center">9 </P>


<p Style='page-break-before:always'>
<HR  SIZE="3" style="COLOR:#999999" WIDTH="100%" ALIGN="CENTER">


 <P STYLE="margin-top:0pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">United Airlines Reports Full-Year and Fourth-Quarter 2016 Performance </P>
<P STYLE="margin-top:12pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman" ALIGN="center"><B>UNITED CONTINENTAL HOLDINGS, INC. </B></P>
<P STYLE="margin-top:0pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman" ALIGN="center">NON-GAAP FINANCIAL RECONCILIATION (Continued) </P> <p STYLE="margin-top:0pt;margin-bottom:0pt ; font-size:8pt">&nbsp;</P>
 <P STYLE="margin-top:0pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">UAL evaluates its financial performance utilizing various accounting principles generally accepted in the
United States of America (GAAP) and <FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">Non-GAAP</FONT> financial measures, including operating income (loss) excluding special charges, income (loss) before income taxes excluding special items, net income (loss)
excluding special items, and net earnings (loss) per share excluding special items, among others. UAL also presented diluted earnings per share excluding special items for the periods presented in 2015 adjusted for the impact of tax expense using
the effective tax rate from the respective period in 2016 in order to make the financial measures more comparable. UAL had minimal income tax expense in the second half of 2015 that was offset by the release of its deferred tax asset valuation
allowance resulting in a net income tax benefit. </P> <P STYLE="font-size:12pt;margin-top:0pt;margin-bottom:0pt">&nbsp;</P>

<p Style='page-break-before:always'>
<HR  SIZE="3" style="COLOR:#999999" WIDTH="100%" ALIGN="CENTER">


 <P STYLE="margin-top:0pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">United Airlines Reports Full-Year and Fourth-Quarter 2016 Performance </P>
<P STYLE="margin-top:12pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman" ALIGN="center"><B>UNITED CONTINENTAL HOLDINGS, INC. </B></P>
<P STYLE="margin-top:0pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman" ALIGN="center">NON-GAAP FINANCIAL RECONCILIATION (Continued) </P> <p STYLE="margin-top:0pt;margin-bottom:0pt ; font-size:8pt">&nbsp;</P>
 <P STYLE="margin-top:0pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">UAL provides financial metrics, including earnings before interest, taxes, depreciation and amortization
(EBITDA) as well as earnings before interest, taxes, depreciation and amortization, and aircraft rent (EBITDAR), that we believe provides useful supplemental information for management and investors by measuring profit and profit as a percentage of
total operating revenues. These financial metrics are adjusted for special items that are <FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">non-recurring</FONT> and that management believes are not indicative of UAL&#146;s ongoing performance. </P>
<P STYLE="font-size:12pt;margin-top:0pt;margin-bottom:0pt">&nbsp;</P>

</TABLE> <P STYLE="margin-top:18pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman"><B><U>Special items </U></B></P>
<P STYLE="margin-top:6pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman"><U>Labor agreement costs and related items:</U> The fleet service, passenger service, storekeeper and other employees represented by the International
Association of Machinists and Aerospace Workers (IAM) ratified seven new contracts with the company which extended the contracts through 2021. The technicians and related employees represented by the International Brotherhood of Teamsters (IBT)
ratified a <FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">six-year</FONT> joint collective bargaining agreement which extended the contract through 2022. During 2016, the company recorded $171&nbsp;million ($110&nbsp;million net of taxes) of special charges
primarily for payments in conjunction with the IAM and IBT agreements described above. As part of the ratified contract with the IBT, the company amended some of its technicians and related employees&#146; postretirement medical plans. The
amendments triggered curtailment accounting, resulting in the recognition of a <FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">one-time</FONT> $60&nbsp;million gain ($38&nbsp;million net of taxes) for accelerated recognition of a prior service credit in one of the
plans. Also, as part of the ratified contract with the Association of Flight Attendants, the company amended two of its flight attendant postretirement medical plans. The amendments triggered curtailment accounting, resulting in the recognition of a
<FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">one-time</FONT> $47&nbsp;million gain ($30&nbsp;million net of taxes) for accelerated recognition of a prior service credit. </P>
<P STYLE="margin-top:12pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman"><U>Severance and benefit costs:</U> During the three months and year ended December&nbsp;31, 2016, the company recorded $10&nbsp;million ($6&nbsp;million net
of taxes) and $37&nbsp;million ($24&nbsp;million net of taxes), respectively, of severance and benefit costs related to a voluntary <FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">early-out</FONT> program for the company&#146;s flight attendants and other
severance agreements. In 2015, the company recorded $107&nbsp;million of severance and benefit costs primarily related to a voluntary <FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">early-out</FONT> program for its flight attendants. In 2014, more than 2,500
flight attendants elected to voluntarily separate from the company for a severance payment, with a maximum value of $100,000 per participant, based on years of service, with retirement dates through the end of 2016. </P>
<P STYLE="margin-top:12pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman"><U>Impairment of assets:</U> In April 2016, the Federal Aviation Administration (FAA) announced that it will designate Newark Liberty International Airport
(Newark) as a Level&nbsp;2 schedule-facilitated airport under the International Air Transport Association Worldwide Slot Guidelines effective October&nbsp;30, 2016. The designation was associated with an updated demand and capacity analysis of
Newark by the FAA. In 2016, the company determined that the FAA&#146;s action impaired the entire value of its Newark slots because the slots are no longer the mechanism that governs <FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">take-off</FONT> and landing
rights. Accordingly, the company recorded a $412&nbsp;million special charge ($264&nbsp;million net of taxes) to write off the intangible asset. During its annual assessment in the fourth quarter of 2015, the company recorded $33&nbsp;million
($22&nbsp;million net of related income tax benefit) related to impairment of its indefinite-lived intangible assets (certain domestic slots and international Pacific routes), $8&nbsp;million for the <FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">write-off</FONT>
of unexercised aircraft purchase options and $7&nbsp;million for inventory held for sale. For the full-year 2015, the company also recorded other impairments, including $10&nbsp;million for discontinued internal software projects and
$10&nbsp;million for the impairment of several engines held for sale. </P> <P STYLE="margin-top:12pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman"><U>Cleveland airport lease restructuring:</U> During 2016, the City of Cleveland
agreed to amend the lease, which runs through 2029, associated with certain excess airport terminal space (principally Terminal D) and related facilities at Hopkins International Airport. The company recorded an accrual for remaining payments
</P>
 <p STYLE="margin-top:0pt;margin-bottom:0pt ; font-size:8pt">&nbsp;</P> <P STYLE="margin-top:0pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman" ALIGN="center">14 </P>


<p Style='page-break-before:always'>
<HR  SIZE="3" style="COLOR:#999999" WIDTH="100%" ALIGN="CENTER">


 <P STYLE="margin-top:0pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">United Airlines Reports Full-Year and Fourth-Quarter 2016 Performance </P>
<p STYLE="margin-top:0pt;margin-bottom:0pt ; font-size:8pt">&nbsp;</P>
 <P STYLE="margin-top:0pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">
under the lease for facilities that the company no longer uses and will continue to incur costs under the lease without economic benefit to the company. This liability was measured and recorded
at its fair value when the company ceased its right to use such facilities leased to it pursuant to the lease. The company recorded a net charge of $74&nbsp;million ($47&nbsp;million net of taxes) related to the amended lease. </P>
<P STYLE="margin-top:12pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman"><U>(Gains) losses on sale of assets and other special charges:</U> During the three months and year ended December&nbsp;31, 2016, the company recorded gains
and losses on sale of assets and other special charges of $19&nbsp;million ($12&nbsp;million net of taxes) and $51&nbsp;million ($33&nbsp;million net of taxes), respectively. During 2015, the company recorded $122&nbsp;million, which includes
$60&nbsp;million of integration-related costs primarily related to systems integration and training for employees, $32&nbsp;million related to charges for legal matters, $16&nbsp;million for the cease use of an aircraft under lease and
$14&nbsp;million for losses on the sale of aircraft and other miscellaneous gains and losses. </P> <P STYLE="margin-top:12pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman"><U>Losses (gain) on extinguishment of debt and other:</U>
During the year ended December&nbsp;31, 2016, the company recorded $8&nbsp;million ($5&nbsp;million net of taxes) of losses due to exchange rate changes in Venezuela applicable to funds held in local currency and recorded a $9&nbsp;million
($6&nbsp;million net of taxes) gain on the sale of an affiliate. During 2015, the company recorded $202&nbsp;million of losses as part of Nonoperating income (expense): Miscellaneous, net due primarily to the
<FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">write-off</FONT> of $134&nbsp;million related to the unamortized <FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">non-cash</FONT> debt discount from the extinguishment of the 6% Notes due 2026 and 6% Notes due 2028, and
$61&nbsp;million of foreign exchange losses on its holdings of Venezuela currency. </P> <P STYLE="margin-top:12pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman"><U>MTM (gains)/losses from fuel derivative contracts settling in
future periods and prior period gains/(losses) on fuel derivative contracts settled in the current period:</U> The company uses certain combinations of derivative contracts that are economic hedges but do not qualify for hedge accounting under U.S.
generally accepted accounting principles. Additionally, the company may enter into contracts at different times and later combine those contracts into structures designated for hedge accounting. As with derivatives that qualify for hedge accounting,
the economic hedges and individual contracts are part of the company&#146;s program to mitigate the adverse financial impact of potential increases in the price of fuel. The company records changes in the fair value of these various contracts that
are not designated for hedge accounting to Nonoperating income (expense): Miscellaneous, net in the statements of consolidated operations. During the three months and year ended December&nbsp;31, 2016, the company did not record any MTM gains or
losses on fuel derivative contracts that will settle in future periods. For fuel derivative contracts that settled in the three months and year ended December&nbsp;31, 2016, the company recorded MTM gains of $4&nbsp;million and $6&nbsp;million,
respectively, in prior periods. During the three months and year ended December&nbsp;31, 2015, the company recorded $1&nbsp;million in MTM losses and $8&nbsp;million in MTM gains, respectively, on fuel derivative contracts that will settle in future
periods. For fuel derivative contracts that settled in the three months and year ended December&nbsp;31, 2015, the company recorded MTM losses of $105&nbsp;million and $241&nbsp;million, respectively, in prior periods. </P>
<P STYLE="margin-top:12pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">(E) The company&#146;s effective tax rate for the three months and year ended December&nbsp;31, 2016 was 55% and 41%, respectively. The rate for both periods
was impacted by a special tax expense of $180&nbsp;million. The company recorded approximately $180&nbsp;million of deferred income tax expense adjustments in AOCI, which related to losses on fuel hedges designated for hedge accounting. Accounting
rules required the adjustments to remain in AOCI as long as the company had fuel derivatives designated for cash flow hedge accounting. In 2016, we settled all of our fuel hedges and have not entered into any new fuel derivative contracts for hedge
accounting. Accordingly, the company reclassified the $180&nbsp;million to income tax expense in 2016. The effective tax rate for 2016 also represented a blend of federal, state and foreign taxes and the impact of certain nondeductible items. </P>
<P STYLE="margin-top:12pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">The company&#146;s effective tax rate for the three months and year ended December&nbsp;31, 2015 was impacted by the valuation allowance release. After
considering all positive and negative evidence, the company concluded that its deferred income taxes would more likely than not be realized. The company released substantially all of&nbsp;its valuation allowance in the third quarter of 2015, which
resulted in a $3.2&nbsp;billion benefit in its provision for income taxes. </P> <P STYLE="margin-top:12pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman" ALIGN="center"># # # </P>
 <p STYLE="margin-top:0pt;margin-bottom:0pt ; font-size:8pt">&nbsp;</P> <P STYLE="margin-top:0pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman" ALIGN="center">15 </P>

 <P STYLE="margin-top:0pt;margin-bottom:0pt" ALIGN="right">


<IMG SRC="g318534g01c33.jpg" ALT="LOGO">
 </P> <p STYLE="margin-top:0pt;margin-bottom:0pt ; font-size:8pt">&nbsp;</P> <P STYLE="margin-top:0pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman"><B><U>Non-Fuel Expense</U>: </B>The guidance provided
in this investor update includes the impact of all labor agreements ratified in 2016, which is expected to add approximately 4 points of impact to unit costs in the first quarter of 2017 and 3 to 4 points of impact to unit costs for the full year of
2017. </P> <P STYLE="margin-top:12pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman"><B><U>Profit Sharing</U>:</B> Due to recently ratified labor agreements, the Company&#146;s profit sharing plans have changed for 2017. The Company
now expects to pay: </P>
<TABLE STYLE="BORDER-COLLAPSE:COLLAPSE; font-family:Times New Roman; font-size:10pt" BORDER="0" CELLPADDING="0" CELLSPACING="0" WIDTH="100%">
<TR>
<TD WIDTH="5%">&nbsp;</TD>
<TD WIDTH="2%" VALIGN="top" ALIGN="left">&#149;</TD>
<TD WIDTH="1%" VALIGN="top">&nbsp;</TD>
<TD ALIGN="left" VALIGN="top">Approximately 7.4% of total adjusted earnings up to a 6.9% adjusted pre-tax margin </TD></TR></TABLE>
<TABLE STYLE="BORDER-COLLAPSE:COLLAPSE; font-family:Times New Roman; font-size:10pt" BORDER="0" CELLPADDING="0" CELLSPACING="0" WIDTH="100%">
<TR>
<TD WIDTH="5%">&nbsp;</TD>
<TD WIDTH="2%" VALIGN="top" ALIGN="left">&#149;</TD>
<TD WIDTH="1%" VALIGN="top">&nbsp;</TD>
<TD ALIGN="left" VALIGN="top">Approximately 13.1% for any adjusted earnings above a 6.9% adjusted pre-tax margin </TD></TR></TABLE>
<TABLE STYLE="BORDER-COLLAPSE:COLLAPSE; font-family:Times New Roman; font-size:10pt" BORDER="0" CELLPADDING="0" CELLSPACING="0" WIDTH="100%">
<TR>
<TD WIDTH="5%">&nbsp;</TD>
<TD WIDTH="2%" VALIGN="top" ALIGN="left">&#149;</TD>
<TD WIDTH="1%" VALIGN="top">&nbsp;</TD>
<TD ALIGN="left" VALIGN="top">Approximately 1.7% for any adjusted earnings above the prior year&#146;s adjusted pre-tax earnings </TD></TR></TABLE> <P STYLE="margin-top:12pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">Adjusted
earnings for the purposes of profit sharing are calculated as GAAP pre-tax earnings, excluding special items, profit sharing expense and share-based compensation program expense. These estimates are consistent with the Company&#146;s current labor
agreements. The Company estimates that share-based compensation expense for the purposes of the profit sharing calculation will be approximately $21 million in the first quarter of 2017. </P>
<P STYLE="margin-top:12pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman"><B><U>Taxes</U>: </B>The Company expects a tax rate of approximately 37% for the first quarter of 2017. However, the Company expects that there will be no
material cash taxes due to United&#146;s net operating loss carryforwards (NOLs), which were approximately $8 billion as of year-end 2015. These NOLs are projected to offset (or minimize) cash income taxes for several years. </P>

<P STYLE="margin-top:0pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman" ALIGN="center">(more) </P>
 <p STYLE="margin-top:0pt;margin-bottom:0pt ; font-size:8pt">&nbsp;</P> <P STYLE="margin-top:0pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman" ALIGN="right">2 </P>


<p Style='page-break-before:always'>
<HR  SIZE="3" style="COLOR:#999999" WIDTH="100%" ALIGN="CENTER">

 <P STYLE="margin-top:0pt;margin-bottom:0pt" ALIGN="right">


<IMG SRC="g318534g01c33.jpg" ALT="LOGO">
 </P> <p STYLE="margin-top:0pt;margin-bottom:0pt ; font-size:8pt">&nbsp;</P> <P STYLE="margin-top:0pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman"><B><U>GAAP to Non-GAAP Reconciliations</U></B> </P>
<P STYLE="margin-top:0pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">UAL is providing guidance utilizing various accounting principles generally accepted in the United States of America (&#147;GAAP&#148;) and Non-GAAP financial
measures, including pre-tax margin, as adjusted, non-operating expense and cost per available seat mile (&#147;CASM&#148;), as adjusted. CASM is a common metric used in the airline industry to measure an airline&#146;s cost structure and efficiency.
UAL reports CASM excluding profit sharing, third-party business expenses, fuel and special charges. Non-GAAP financial measures are presented because they provide management and investors the ability to measure and monitor UAL&#146;s performance on
a consistent basis. </P> <P STYLE="margin-top:12pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">Pursuant to SEC Regulation G, UAL has included the following reconciliation of reported Non-GAAP financial measures to comparable
financial measures reported on a GAAP basis. </P> <P STYLE="margin-top:12pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">UAL believes excluding profit sharing allows investors to better understand and analyze our recurring cost
performance and provides a more meaningful comparison of our core operating costs to the airline industry. UAL believes that adjusting for special charges is useful to investors because they are non-recurring charges not indicative of UAL&#146;s
ongoing performance. UAL also believes that excluding third-party business expenses, such as maintenance, ground handling and catering services for third parties, fuel sales and non-air mileage redemptions, provides more meaningful disclosure
because these expenses are not directly related to UAL&#146;s core business. UAL believes that excluding fuel costs from certain measures is useful to investors because it provides an additional measure of management&#146;s performance excluding the
effects of a significant cost item over which management has limited influence. In addition, UAL believes that excluding non-cash (gains)/losses on fuel derivative contracts from non-operating expense is useful because it allows investors to better
understand the impact of settled hedges on a given period&#146;s results. </P> <P STYLE="font-size:12pt;margin-top:0pt;margin-bottom:0pt">&nbsp;</P>
<TABLE CELLSPACING="0" CELLPADDING="0" WIDTH="100%" BORDER="0" STYLE="BORDER-COLLAPSE:COLLAPSE; font-family:Times New Roman; font-size:10pt" ALIGN="center">


<TR>
<TD WIDTH="89%"></TD>
<TD VALIGN="bottom" WIDTH="1%"></TD>
<TD></TD>
<TD></TD>
<TD></TD>
<TD VALIGN="bottom" WIDTH="1%"></TD>
<TD></TD>
<TD></TD>
<TD></TD>
<TD VALIGN="bottom" WIDTH="1%"></TD>
<TD></TD>
